<div id="review_1374710127" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1374710127" />
    <a title="Rebecca (whymermaids)" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/4713345-rebecca-whymermaids"><img alt="Rebecca (whymermaids)" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1482761193p2/4713345.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1374710127?book_show_action=true">Aug 26, 2015</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rebecca (whymermaids)" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rebecca (whymermaids)" href="/user/show/4713345-rebecca-whymermaids">Rebecca (whymermaids)</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was ok"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was ok</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1374710127" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer17900173394528393679">I wanted to like this book, I really did. I’d heard such raving reviews from some of my friends about it, and I was intrigued by the idea of a thriller set on the moon. What could the premise possibly be? Aliens? Astronauts gone rogue? I was excited to find out. <br/><br/>And then I started reading it.<br/><br/>The premise of 172 Hours on the Moon boils down to: there’s something dangerous and weird happening on the moon, and NASA has kept silent about it for fifty years, but now it’s back and they need to fix it. </span>
  <span id="freeText17900173394528393679" style="display:none">I wanted to like this book, I really did. I’d heard such raving reviews from some of my friends about it, and I was intrigued by the idea of a thriller set on the moon. What could the premise possibly be? Aliens? Astronauts gone rogue? I was excited to find out. <br /><br />And then I started reading it.<br /><br />The premise of 172 Hours on the Moon boils down to: there’s something dangerous and weird happening on the moon, and NASA has kept silent about it for fifty years, but now it’s back and they need to fix it. To build popularity and hopefully gain support (read: $), they decide to make it a big spectacle: the 50th anniversary of the first Lunar Landing, using models that look like those from Apollo 11. Oh, and did I mention their plan involved sending teenagers to space?<br /><br />Dumb.<br /><br />This is where my problems began, and despite my hopes they’d get better, they didn’t.<br /><br />So NASA, this big giant space organization that has LITERALLY put man on the moon, that employs some of the SMARTEST people on the planet and has a contingency plan for their contingency plan, decides it’s going to hold a lottery and choose three teenagers from around the world to send to space. <br /><br />That’s right. THREE. <br /><br />The application said they needed to be in good health, etc, but there were no tests actually required, no fitness evaluation or mental stress tests. No knowledge of space or science required. <br /><br />So… you’re telling me that out of the entire world, NASA just happened to RANDOMLY pick three teenagers to go to space and all three of them are perfectly fit to go? <br /><br />No.<br /><br />(also, they all speak English, I’m assuming, since they communicate without effort amongst one another despite their different countries of origin?)<br /><br />If I’d been in charge at NASA, I would’ve put in place some evaluation they had to pass before they could even apply. THEN I would’ve chosen 50 or so candidates who scored the highest (on a range of tests - physical, mental, stress, etc) and maybe even dreamed of becoming astronauts (instead of going because they wanted to get a girl back, ugh), and then made them go through even more tests to whittle it down to the final three. Think The Selection/The Bachelor meets Armageddon. <br /><br />But hell, if I were in charge at NASA, I wouldn’t be sending teenagers to space. Or really, I wouldn’t be doing anything from this dumb book.<br /><br />So they get to the moon. Our three main teenagers aren’t particularly interesting, and the events on the moon sound like The Martian but way less smart and with some weird “thing” killing people. Even the deaths were boring.<br /><br />Idk. I thought the “thing” (no spoilers) was pretty dumb and if they knew that much about it beforehand, it seems pretty reckless to send people up there without any methods of taking care of it. Maybe let your peeps know there’s something out to get them instead of keeping it a secret? You know, to protect their lives on THE MOON. <br /><br />Half of what happened on the moon didn’t even make sense, and I just really wanted more development of what could have been a really cool idea. <br /><br />The scariest part about this was the urban legend one of the characters tells that has nothing to do with the plot. Cool story, bro.<br /><br />Anyway. This is more of a ranty ramble than a well structured review and I apologize for that. But this was just dumb and made me dumber for having read it. <br /><br />2/5 stars for what it could’ve been with a better (or even just adult) writer, and for the fact that I did finish it and was mildly intrigued at times.<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="17900173394528393679" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1026709306" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1026709306" />
    <a title="Rachel" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3628969-rachel"><img alt="Rachel" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1587731574p2/3628969.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1026709306?book_show_action=true">Aug 14, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Rachel" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Rachel" href="/user/show/3628969-rachel">Rachel</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

          <span class="greyText">&nbsp;&middot;&nbsp;</span>
          <a class="lightGreyText" title="Hardcover 9780316182881" href="/book/show/12860573-172-hours-on-the-moon">review of another edition</a>


        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/3628969-rachel?shelf=read-2015">read-2015</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1026709306" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer8254249529166270115"><b>*1.5 stars*</b><br/>Wow so I was really disappointed in this. Basically all I got out of it was an attempt at a cheap thrill / "crazy plot twist" at the end, but I wasn't even impressed by that. Usually when I don't like a book I try and give it the whole "oh maybe it's just me" deal, but I just don't think this was a well crafted novel.<br/><br/><b>Plot-</b> Essentially, nothing happens in this book until the last 50ish pages. Obviously I'm exaggerating, but what I really mean is nothing of importance happens. I feel li</span>
  <span id="freeText8254249529166270115" style="display:none"><b>*1.5 stars*</b><br />Wow so I was really disappointed in this. Basically all I got out of it was an attempt at a cheap thrill / "crazy plot twist" at the end, but I wasn't even impressed by that. Usually when I don't like a book I try and give it the whole "oh maybe it's just me" deal, but I just don't think this was a well crafted novel.<br /><br /><b>Plot-</b> Essentially, nothing happens in this book until the last 50ish pages. Obviously I'm exaggerating, but what I really mean is nothing of importance happens. I feel like all the author cared about was the end, so he wrote that, then realized, oh yeah I have to actually get them to the moon somehow, I guess I'll write that, and throw in a little bit of "foreshadowing." If you really want to know what the twist ending is, you could honestly just pick up the book and read only the last 100 pages, and you probably wouldn't even be confused, because the pages before didn't set up anything important except for the reason the kids are up there, and the names of the characters- both of which are in the synopsis so you could just read that and be covered. As a result of this, I was so incredibly bored throughout this entire book, even the end. I'll admit, I only kept reading because I wanted to know what this "crazy ending" everyone talks about was, and I even thought that was lame. Yeah, yeah the ending was sort of creepy, but it wasn't nearly as scary or mind-blowing as I was expecting, and I predicted it long before it actually happened. I can see that the idea of the twist was original (which is basically the only reason I'm giving it an extra half star), but I don't think it was executed well at all, and I really was not impressed.<br /><br /><b>Writing-</b> I don't know if the author is a bad writer, or if the translation was just bad, but this writing really just wasn't good. The dialogue didn't sound natural, the descriptions lacked "oomph," and the writing just felt very bland and juvenile.<br /><br /><b>Characters-</b> Wow, look at that, the characters were terribly underdeveloped and not written well, just like the rest of this book! Sorry, too much? I just didn't find myself enjoying any aspect of this book. The characters were so incredibly flat, and most of the time I couldn't tell the two girl main characters apart. They had no development what so ever, and I feel like they were just placeholders, and it didn't matter who the characters of the story were, as long as they were affected by "the twist." I know I'm being really harsh but these were seriously some of the worst characters I've read about in a long time. The writer did attempt to give them some background as to why they wanted to go to the moon, but it didn't feel real, and it wasn't written into the story well either, it was just handed to us like, "here's some character information I'm obligated to give to you!"<br /><br /><b>Overall-</b> I don't think there was one thing I enjoyed about this book, honestly. Okay, I think the only thing I liked was one particular scene, just because it was the first hint of creepiness in the book and it gave me hope, but I truly think that's the only thing. I thought this was a very poorly done "horror" novel that was so dependent on its twist at the end that everything else in the novel was just put on the sidelines, including what was happening in the plot up to the twist. Even with that being said, this still could have been a 2 star book if the twist and ending was done well, but it wasn't, so I can't afford it any more stars than the one I am giving it.<br /><br /><b>Recommend?-</b> Not at all.</span>
  <a data-text-id="8254249529166270115" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_478974580" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/478974580" />
    <a title="B" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/5206717-b"><img alt="B" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/f_50x66-6a03a5c12233c941481992b82eea8d23.png" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/478974580?book_show_action=true">Dec 16, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="B" class="user" itemprop="url" name="B" href="/user/show/5206717-b">B</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=clever-plot-twists">clever-plot-twists</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=deserves-the-hype">deserves-the-hype</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=judge-a-book-by-the-cover">judge-a-book-by-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=creeeeepy">creeeeepy</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=this-book-and-i-are-eloping">this-book-and-i-are-eloping</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=read-reviewed">read-reviewed</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2013-favorites">2013-favorites</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=2013-reads">2013-reads</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=awesome-world-building">awesome-world-building</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/5206717-b?shelf=didn-t-see-that-coming">didn-t-see-that-coming</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer478974580" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3409982341678869044"><i>Actual rating is 3.5 stars</i><br/><br/>Yesterday, I watched The Blair Witch Project for the first time since its release fourteen years ago. Now, for those of you who still haven't seen The Blair Witch Project and know not much about it, what tends to either make or break the film for people is the fact that it keeps the audience almost entirely in the dark in regards to its titular witch. The purpose of this is to have the viewers illustrate their own image of the witch in their heads, thereby establishing </span>
  <span id="freeText3409982341678869044" style="display:none"><i>Actual rating is 3.5 stars</i><br /><br />Yesterday, I watched The Blair Witch Project for the first time since its release fourteen years ago. Now, for those of you who still haven't seen The Blair Witch Project and know not much about it, what tends to either make or break the film for people is the fact that it keeps the audience almost entirely in the dark in regards to its titular witch. The purpose of this is to have the viewers illustrate their own image of the witch in their heads, thereby establishing that, in the end, a viewer's imagination can be scarier than anything presented to them in film. <br /><br />In the same vein, 172 Hours on the Moon is like The Blair Witch Project. Johan Harstad keeps us all in the dark until the very end of the novel (which I suppose is a step up from TBWP, considering there are no answers given at the end of that), and sometimes, it's frustrating. More often than not, it reads like that one boyfriend in many crappy paranormal romances; you know, the one that keeps vital information from the MC because "she's not ready for it," or "it's too dangerous"? <br /><br />Or, some scientist is about to give us answers, but he's cut off abruptly and doesn't finish his sentence. However, with that having been said, I am really glad Harstad chose this method of storytelling for 172 Hours on the Moon, because all of the events are only made that much scarier when you truly have no idea what is performing said events. <br /><br />And as for 172 Hours being scary, it's scary. Frightening. Horrifying. Downright chilling. Disquieting. <br /><br />All of the above. <br /><br />Granted, how horrifying I think this novel is may be biased, considering the fact that the thought of space in and of itself makes me feel short of breath, but looking at other reviews, I'm not sure that's the case. No matter what you're afraid of or not afraid of, 172 Hours seems to have struck a nerve with nearly every reader. <br /><blockquote>"In space no one can hear you scream."<br />- Alien (1979)</blockquote><br />While the daunting nature of Harstad's writing style was certainly not something that was lost in translation, I think that the quality of the character development may have been. Or maybe genuine character and relationship development was never something in the novel to begin with, but either way, I think it's safe to say I didn't care about any of the characters in 172 Hours. In fact, if I wasn't assured by many that the last half is scary, I likely would have DNF'd at some point in the first half. <br /><br />172 Hours is a novel that requires two things: patience, and suspension of disbelief. For about half of the novel, the three teenagers aren't even on the moon yet. And if you, like me, do not care for the characters, the first half may be a bumpy ride. Also, why is NASA bringing three teenagers to the moon, when it's known that there is something highly dangerous on the moon? *shrug* We're given a pretty shitty explanation, and you kind of just have to just go with it. <br /><br />I promise you, regardless of whether or not you're afraid of space, or the moon, there will be something in 172 Hours on the Moon to unsettle you at the very least. The way Johan Harstad describes the barren landscape of the moon, the scary stories scared amongst the three teenagers, and of course, the villain, is sure to scare the crap out of you. And odds are you'll enjoy being scared, because no matter what, 172 Hours on the Moon is a fun and deeply chilling read, and once you get past the nitty gritty, you won't be able to put it down (regardless how much you may want to, so that you can take a breather and turn on a light).</span>
  <a data-text-id="3409982341678869044" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_457644010" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/457644010" />
    <a title="Peeves" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3839297-peeves"><img alt="Peeves" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1330077066p2/3839297.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">

<span id="freeTextContainer14483902923258267598"><b>SAY WHAT???</b><br/><br/>Really. That was my exact reaction when i finished the book. It is creepy to say the least. It scared the hibbie jibbies out of me and i truly and madly was convinced for a moment that the Moon might actually be hell.<br/><br/>I am glad i read the book because i learned a couple of new things (<i> like where the phrase "Houston, we have a problem" originated from. <s>yeah because that is totally important for me to suceed in life</s> </i>.) The premise is effing great which is what made me pick up the book i</span>
  <span id="freeText14483902923258267598" style="display:none"><b>SAY WHAT???</b><br /><br />Really. That was my exact reaction when i finished the book. It is creepy to say the least. It scared the hibbie jibbies out of me and i truly and madly was convinced for a moment that the Moon might actually be hell.<br /><br />I am glad i read the book because i learned a couple of new things (<i> like where the phrase "Houston, we have a problem" originated from. <s>yeah because that is totally important for me to suceed in life</s> </i>.) The premise is effing great which is what made me pick up the book in the first place but seriously? poor execution. POOOOOOOR EXECUTION. (To be continued)<br /><br />Question: is it because the book is translated that it didn’t feel authentic? is that fair for the author? Damn i wish i knew Norwegian Lang.<br /><br />(Continued)The book is set in the moon. Okay the second half at least. NASA allows three teenagers Mia, Midori and Antonio to go on the trip to gain publicity(for what? we don't know.) It could have been so much more but it was not. Alot of things were left unexplained. We never get to see what Sander(Mia's brother) wrote in that letter to Mia. We never know what happens to Simone(Antonio's Ex-gf).We don't know why this scary evil space-moon doppelgangers are called 6EQUJ5. We don't know why the Doppelgangers don't allow the Astronauts to leave the moon. We don’t.. Oh why do i bother? But wait!<br /><br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[Okay so someone please explain because i really want to know why the author makes us read the entire last chunk about Mia and Midori fighting the doppelgangers on the way to evacuation pod in Darlah 1 when i actual truth as we are revealed to in the last page that Mia actually suicided at nice cozy little spot outside Darlah 2?<br /><br />And and and... Why does the Doppelganger think "Yes i am finally home"?<br />I thought they were meant to be undisturbed on the moon?<br /><br /><br />URGHHHH. SO MANY QUESTIONS. TOO MANY QUESTIONS. Hence the awkward two stars. There my friends, a great opportunity for a awesome book to be written has been lost due to poor execution, very shallow development of characters(cardinal sin!)and a very confusing ending.<br /><br />p/s: Does anyone else find it weird that Neil Armstrong, the first person to step on the moon has been mysteriously ignored in the book?<br /> <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span></span>

<div id="review_701144757" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/701144757" />
    <a title="Sarah Churchill" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/18321322-sarah-churchill"><img alt="Sarah Churchill" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1489514919p2/18321322.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/701144757?book_show_action=true">Aug 22, 2013</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Sarah Churchill" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Sarah Churchill" href="/user/show/18321322-sarah-churchill">Sarah Churchill</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer701144757" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3722720273874333036">WHAAAAAAAAT?!<br/><br/>I'm a little torn with this one. It wasn't perfect - I didn't like the characters all that much, and all of them were 100% stereotypes. It was fairly predictable in places, but importantly the ENDING was not. I just stared at the last page for a good couple of minutes trying to get my head around what I'd just read. <br/><br/>I found it pretty slow for the first half of the book. I got the characters mixed up because they were flat representations of teenagers that I didn't really care for, e</span>
  <span id="freeText3722720273874333036" style="display:none">WHAAAAAAAAT?!<br /><br />I'm a little torn with this one. It wasn't perfect - I didn't like the characters all that much, and all of them were 100% stereotypes. It was fairly predictable in places, but importantly the ENDING was not. I just stared at the last page for a good couple of minutes trying to get my head around what I'd just read. <br /><br />I found it pretty slow for the first half of the book. I got the characters mixed up because they were flat representations of teenagers that I didn't really care for, each a walking, talking stereotype of their respective countries. And the love story is both unnecessary and unbelievable <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[(but thankfully also short-lived) <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. BUT the overall premise and execution when they actually got to the moon was great.<br /><br />I liked that everything wasn't spelled out for me as a reader - I hate it when I'm reading a book and it's practically hitting me over the head going "did you get that? Did you get that bit? Aren't I awesome?!" This was far more subtle with its twists, which is great because you have to pay attention and your imagination runs wild. Towards the end I was seeing twists where there was none, and realising one had happened too late and had to flip back through the pages to find it. <br /><br />So, for me the overall experience of this book outweighed the nagging issues I had with it, and I'm really glad I read it. I'd recommend it to anyone who likes to mix a bit of horror in with their sci-fi, and wouldn't be surprised to see a film adaptation happen.</span>
  <a data-text-id="3722720273874333036" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer272790404" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4872853760457399840"><a href='http://laurenreadsya.tumblr.com/post/100926215447/review-172-hours-on-the-moon-by-johan-harstad' rel='nofollow noopener'>Read my full review on Lauren Reads YA (with GIFs and pretty book photography!)</a><br/><br/>Imagine if a horror book and a science fiction book made a book baby… 172 Hours on the Moon is that baby.<br/><br/>All I knew about this book before going in was that it was creepy, and I’m so glad I didn’t know any more. That made the twists even more exciting! The first half of the book I was thinking of all kinds of crazy (conspiracy) theories, and once you find out what the twist is, you’re like, "WHAT?!"<br/><br/><img src='https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414262400ra/11631825.gif' class='gr-hostedUserImg'/><br/><br/>The only thing that</span>
  <span id="freeText4872853760457399840" style="display:none"><a href="http://laurenreadsya.tumblr.com/post/100926215447/review-172-hours-on-the-moon-by-johan-harstad" rel="nofollow noopener">Read my full review on Lauren Reads YA (with GIFs and pretty book photography!)</a><br><br>Imagine if a horror book and a science fiction book made a book baby… 172 Hours on the Moon is that baby.<br><br>All I knew about this book before going in was that it was creepy, and I’m so glad I didn’t know any more. That made the twists even more exciting! The first half of the book I was thinking of all kinds of crazy (conspiracy) theories, and once you find out what the twist is, you’re like, "WHAT?!"<br><br><img src="https://images.gr-assets.com/hostedimages/1414262400ra/11631825.gif" class="gr-hostedUserImg"><br><br>The only thing that made me give this 4.5 instead of 5 is the blandness of the characters. The three main characters were all very stereotypical, and I felt myself caring more for the secondary characters. And God, Mia was annoying in the beginning! Girl, your band is never going to get anywhere… Also, stop acting like you’re too cool for space. *hand emoji*<br><br>This book gets ALL THE EXTRA POINTS because it made me SO EXCITED ABOUT SPACE. Even if there’s something terrifying in space (on the moon, to be specific). Just… SPACE!!!<br><br>After finishing it late in the evening, I spent the rest of the night reading about the Apollo 11 conspiracies and learning about how to do your business in space and basically watched everything available on SciShow Space. I think the fact that this book made me excited about space is so important, and everyone with even a slight interest in science should check this out.<br><br>I was so creeped out by the whole thing and the ending was absolutely MIND-BLOWING. I’ve read a few books since then and still find myself thinking about this one pretty regularly. I highly recommend 172 Hours on the Moon. What a page-turner!</span>

<div id="review_812402804" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/812402804" />
    <a title="Christina" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/9403772-christina"><img alt="Christina" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1464276927p2/9403772.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/812402804?book_show_action=true">Jan 04, 2014</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Christina" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Christina" href="/user/show/9403772-christina">Christina</a>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>

        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer812402804" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4306470865855607389">This book was literally insane. It was strictly a horror novel. I don't usually get so unsettled by any type of "horror" novel, but <b>this book scared the shit out of me</b>. (I also read basically all of this book around 1 AM so that probably contributed to the fact that it freaked me out.)<br/><br/>Anyway, the first 100 pages or so weren't the most interesting. I think they were supposed to help us get to know NASA's mission and the characters better but both of those, for me, were severely underdeveloped. Ho</span>
  <span id="freeText4306470865855607389" style="display:none">This book was literally insane. It was strictly a horror novel. I don't usually get so unsettled by any type of "horror" novel, but <b>this book scared the shit out of me</b>. (I also read basically all of this book around 1 AM so that probably contributed to the fact that it freaked me out.)<br /><br />Anyway, the first 100 pages or so weren't the most interesting. I think they were supposed to help us get to know NASA's mission and the characters better but both of those, for me, were severely underdeveloped. However, as soon as everyone got to the Moon, I definitely began to enjoy the book and I couldn't put it down.<br /><br />I also felt like the execution of the plot was lacking in this book. I don't think some pieces of information were presented well. But, after reading that last chapter, I actually think that might have been intentional on the author's part.<br />This book will probably freak you out.<br />It will confuse you.<br />You will not know right from wrong.<br />If you want a good scare that will cause you to contemplate a few things you thought you were certain about before, Read. This. Book.<br /><br />Just a question I have for everyone that has read the book: (SPOILERS)<br /><a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[So, as Mia was struggling to get into the escape pod at DARLAH 1, how exactly did the POV change to her evil doppelgänger as we saw "her" get to escape??? <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span><br />I STILL HAVE SO MANY QUESTIONS!</span>
  <a data-text-id="4306470865855607389" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>


      <div class="reviewFooter uitext buttons">

<div class=" clearFloats bigBox"><div class="h2Container gradientHeaderContainer"><h2 class="brownBackground">Readers also enjoyed</h2></div><div class="bigBoxBody"><div class="bigBoxContent containerWithHeaderContent"><div class='bookCarousel'>
<div class='carouselRow' style='width: 3600px'>
<ul>
<li class='cover' id='bookCover_26153925'>
<a href="https://www.goodreads.com/book/show/26153925-with-malice"><img alt="With Malice" src="https://i.gr-assets.com/images/S/compressed.photo.goodreads.com/books/1465546059l/26153925._SX98_.jpg" />
</a>

  
<script type="text/javascript" charset="utf-8">
//<![CDATA[  

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('yJjAeUUI6sjLIw2rXGSk3rs6gjS63bUgiBGd+USHszbiMtgXnO/idte+OhdAEQOe/xrgWtfwMUukQxv0FoSblg==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {
    new Ajax.Updater('addGroupBooks' + book_id + '', '/group/add_book_box', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){refreshGroupBoxComplete(request, book_id);}, parameters:'id=' + group_id + '&book_id=' + book_id + '&refresh=true' + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('YGUHilzdj/twz30hr7O+qG/vvqvKAjR7aoqamgh3CJBKzx/khTqHRWxSSp2zxhnoK8/cxacvsBBG2ByXWnQgMA==')})
  }
//]]>
</script>

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer11553051359210036895">Johan Harstad is a Norwegian author, graphic designer, playwright, drummer, and international sensation. He is the winner of the 2008 Brage Award (Brageprisen), previously won by Per Petterson, and his books have been published in over 11 countries. In 2009, he was named the first ever in-house playwright at the National Theatre in Oslo. His first novel <i>Buzz Aldrin, What Happened To You In All The</i></span>
  <span id="freeText11553051359210036895" style="display:none">Johan Harstad is a Norwegian author, graphic designer, playwright, drummer, and international sensation. He is the winner of the 2008 Brage Award (Brageprisen), previously won by Per Petterson, and his books have been published in over 11 countries. In 2009, he was named the first ever in-house playwright at the National Theatre in Oslo. His first novel <i>Buzz Aldrin, What Happened To You In All The Confusion</i>, originally published in Norway by Gyldendal in 2005, was made into a TV series in 2009 starring The Wire’s Chad Coleman. Harstad lives in Oslo.</span>
